noncomputable def f_M (R M : Real) (f : Complex ‚Üí Complex) : Complex ‚Üí Complex :=
  fun z => (f z / z) / ((2 * M : Complex) - f z)

lemma lem_g_analytic (R M : Real) (hR : R > 0) (hM : M > 0) (f : Complex ‚Üí Complex)
    (hf : AnalyticOn ‚ÑÇ f {z : Complex | norm z ‚â§ R})
    (hf0 : f 0 = 0) (hfRe : ‚àÄ z : Complex, norm z ‚â§ R ‚Üí (f z).re ‚â§ M) :
    AnalyticOn ‚ÑÇ (f_M R M f) {z : Complex | norm z ‚â§ R} := by
  unfold f_M
  -- f_M = (f z / z) / (2*M - f z)
  -- First show f z / z is analytic
  have h1 := lem_removable_singularity R hR f hf hf0
  -- Then show 2*M - f z is analytic and nonzero
  have h2 : AnalyticOn ‚ÑÇ (fun z => (2 * M : Complex) - f z) {z : Complex | norm z ‚â§ R} := by
    apply AnalyticOn.sub
    ¬∑ exact analyticOn_const
    ¬∑ exact hf
  have h3 := lem_denominator_nonzero R M hR hM f hf hfRe
  -- Finally, quotient of analytic functions with nonzero denominator is analytic
  exact lem_quotient_analytic R hR (fun z => f z / z) (fun z => (2 * M : Complex) - f z) h1 h2 h3

**Considering analytic methods**

It seems that lem_removable_singularity is necessary to prove f_M is analytic, so we can't just remove it. We might need to prove it instead or adjust lem_g_analytic. For closed disks, we could keep the domain to z ‚â† 0, but the quotient lemma includes 0. A piecewise definition for f_M might fix the non-analytic issue, albeit it's a more intrusive change. Adjusting lem_g_analytic for a "punctured disk" could be a solution instead.
**Exploring analytic definitions**

I‚Äôm considering replacing the proof of lem_removable_singularity with a result from Mathlib, involving the lemma `AnalyticAt.div`, which requires the denominator to be nonzero at the point. Since we have f(0) = 0, it allows for the possibility that g(z) = f(z)/z is analytic on the set minus 0, maybe even analyticWithinAt at 0. The definition of AnalyticWithinAt involves having an analytic function in a neighborhood that matches f on a particular intersection. I‚Äôm still working through the details!
**Considering domain restrictions**

I'm exploring an approach where instead of proving full AnalyticOn on a closed disk, I could restrict it to the set where 0 < ‚Äñz‚Äñ ‚â§ R and leave out 0. However, some later lemmas seem to rely on the full domain. They involve using `lem_quotient_analytic R hR (fun z => f z / z)`, which only requires AnalyticOn in that domain. This could limit the flexibility if I restrict it, leading to wider code changes. I could instead modify lem_g_analytic to not require the numerator to be analytic at 0.
**Addressing analytic issues**

I‚Äôm grappling with proving `AnalyticOn ‚ÑÇ (fun z => f z / z)` over the set where ‚Äñz‚Äñ ‚â§ R, given hf and hf0. I wonder if there's a Mathlib theorem regarding `AnalyticAt` at zero based on the `HasDerivAt` properties of f. To show analyticWithinAt at 0, I could try rewriting it as `ContinuousAt` plus differentiability, but I know analytic requires more. Since f is analyticOn a non-open set, I should show `AnalyticAt ‚ÑÇ f 0`. Although 0 lies in the closed disk, I'm not quite sure how to align everything properly.
**Clarifying analytic properties**

I‚Äôm trying to understand that while `AnalyticOn` might not guarantee analytic properties at interior points within a closed set, it does require analytic properties in neighborhoods. The definition of `AnalyticOn` says it involves `AnalyticAt` for every point in a set. If `AnalyticOn ‚ÑÇ f {z | ‚Äñz‚Äñ ‚â§ R}` holds, it also means `AnalyticAt` at every point, including 0. We could explore if `fun z => f z / z` is analyticWithinAt at 0, potentially using theorems from Mathlib. I‚Äôll need to verify these connections further!
